Strategic Interpretation

Careharaclen’s adaptive forest plains approach won because the finish was decided by treasury, not territory, and its 200 total outweighed Yunavaun Chiefdom’s 52 even though the runner-up had no regions left. The board’s earlier regional swings mattered less because the mid and late economic shifts created a resource edge that became central to the finish, which meant map control alone could not convert into victory. Liniunarri’s expansionist push and the later Careharaclen territorial lead both failed to settle the game because the ring remained economically contestable, so that income accumulation ultimately separated the winner.
The closest challenger was Yunavaun Chiefdom (Adaptive Forest) at 52 treasury and 0 regions.
Yunavaun Chiefdom remained locked in a claim dispute with Liniunarri over 2 regions dominated by Yunavaun communities.
Careharaclen treated Liniunarri as a peer-state rival, with both polities reading each other as serious strategic threats.

Victor's History

Careharaclen’s victory was not a matter of spectacle but of conversion: its Adaptive Forest Plains approach turned early pressure into lasting strength, and by turn 100 it stood first with 9 regions and a treasury of 200. It opened with 18 attack attempts, contested neighboring borders immediately, and then built steadily through the middle and late phases, where the decisive economic edge emerged. The rivals who briefly led in regions could not sustain that position, while the Yunavaun Chiefdom in particular rose and then fell away entirely after 53 attacks. In the end, the record favors disciplined accumulation over fleeting territorial advantage, and Careharaclen understood that balance better than any other faction.
